<Time>1544587724539< /Time><rate>5<//rate>< Review>
Okay, this is a fast food pizzeria. It is fast, it is hot, it is filling and tastes reasonably good (better than Domino's IMHO.) They have bottled soft drinks and water, including 2 liter bottles. They do not have cups or forks or knives. The place is clean and parking is never a challenge. Close to hwy 101 at Tefft exit. So if you're hungry and in a hurry, it's a good choice. If you're looking for gourmet Pizza, I recommend Klondikes in Arroyo Grande. Or, right across the street is Me n Ed's Pizzeria, a local favorite with top-notch pizza and other excellent fare.<//Review>

< review>
Be carefull  when buying engines from this shop learn from my mistake.
So here's the story, I called them and asked about an engine I've asked how many miles does the ENGINE have now I've specified that i want to know the mileage of the engine. I was told that the engine has 30k miles so I blindly trusted this shop and took their word for it. After bringing the engine home I ran the vin number and it turns out the engine had over 150k mils on it. So I went back to get my refund and talk to them about it.
First they didn't even want to give me a refund even tho the receipt said that I have 10 days to return it so it looks like they don't even know their own policies. After I handed them the recipe I told them that they told me the incorrect mileage and their response was that they get miles from the vehicle rather then the  engine which then it clicked to me that they can just lie about how many miles the engine actually has. Rather then being honest they just lie about it give you a lower mileage and when u complain or look up the vin number they protect themselves by saying that they get the mileage from the vehicle or what auctions tells them. It took me 30 seconds to look up the vin number of the engine I'm sure that a practice that they can integrate into there business practice but who needs to be honest to there costumers when u can lie and make more money. Also they'll charge u a 25% restocking fee so which for me was $160.
I'd avoid this shop if your looking for an honest business but if you have to make sure to request the vin number of the engine and not the car. You would think that a shop of this size would be able to afford carfax account but what who needs that anyways. Also side no the will take 5 bucks of your invoice if you give them a 5 star review so they basically bough their reviews.< /review>

<user_id>107836358820840066342</user_id><user_name>Ben Xie<//user_name>< time>
1527063979989<//time>
<rating>4</rating><text>Bought a car from here about a year ago so I've had time to look over the car with a fine tooth comb. I'll start by saying that I am a car guy, I'm that person in the family that reads the car magazines, does minor car stuff for friends and family, does the research and negotiations on new cars, etc.

When I first approached Car Star, it was to look at a 2008 Lexus. I called and was told it was available. When I got there, I was told it sold earlier and that the person I talked to on the phone had already gone home and wouldn't have been aware of the sale. So, I have to ding them for this since this can easily be construed as a bait and switch. It's not a huge lot, that guy should have known and/or double checked.

I made them pull a 2010 off a pedestal for me to look at instead. It was pretty dark already and I didn't get to do a thorough mechanical inspection, but the deal was fair and everybody was straightforward. I had a couple snags to work through on my end, and they worked with me to get through it, so I felt ok going ahead with the purchase anyway. They put on a little pressure trying to sell the warranty but that's expected. Otherwise, pretty smooth transaction and no complaints.

A year later, the car has been mostly fine. I will caution buyers to do their own mechanical inspections, bring it to someone you trust instead of relying on their mechanic. The salesman specifically told me it was inspected and got an oil change. I can tell you for sure that my vehicle hadn't had its oil changed in a while - the oil was much darker than the new oil I put in 500 miles later. < Review>
Purchased here exactly 5 years ago and the rent has gone up almost $500 a month in 5 years. Buyers beware. We all just got notified today of a new rent increase (mine $140 a mo.) which takes effect Nov. 1st 2019 (how heartless of the owners of the park to raise the rent right at the holidays) It went up $140 a mo. last Nov. 1st as well. There is no rent control here and the sky is the limit as to how much, and how often they can raise your rent. Management fails to respond to concerns about park violations. They ignore them and don't enforce them. People have been camping out in tents on the front porch of their homes, there are several people living in small trailers, visitor parking spots are constantly being filled by family members of owners who have multiple cars and tenants. RV's can come and go several times a month in the empty lots so you can purchase a home here, pay $2500+ a mo. and RV's can come in & out of the vacant lot next door to you for several years. This place has become a very expensive campground. My next door neighbor recently removed an approximate 6 ft. portion of our bordering fence without permission to erect a giant storage shed that crosses our property line into my yard. It's combustable material and way to close to my home and my daughter's bedroom. I notified the park, they did NOTHING, I contacted the housing department and they cited the homeowner and the park and have ordered it to be dismantled and removed. Now the park is retaliating against me. Do your research. I have evidence, photos, video recordings, and every e-mail I have sent the park to inform them of violations which they have ignored. This is written based on facts, not emotions. You will have no protection from very high, yearly rent increases and your property value will diminish with RV's and tents among owned homes.<//Review>
